Free Talk by Ke Tong

A Laughing Matter 127

·Hai· Ke

Mother (to her eight-year-old daughter): You, girl, don't you know how to be clean at all? When I give you a bath, you try to hide and dodge as if you're avoiding a debt.

Daughter: Mother, you're so rough and heavy-handed. You scrub me until my skin is sore and itchy. I don't want to take a bath anymore.

Mother: If you're living under my care, I have to give you a bath every day. See where you can hide.

Daughter: Then I'll get married tomorrow.

A: Do you know Lao Bing?

B: I know him.

A: He asked me for money yesterday. Do you think I should lend it to him? Do you know his background?

B: I know him. I know him as well as I know you. He has absolutely no credit.

An old teacher lecturing a class of female students: As women, you should obey your parents at home. After you get married, you should obey your husband. This is the natural order of things and cannot be violated.

A female student: Excuse me, teacher, how should we obey our husband?

Old teacher: What the ancients said, "the husband sings, the wife follows," that's what obedience means.

A female student: Teacher, what if the husband is mute and cannot sing? How can the wife follow?

Old teacher: Not only that, wherever the husband goes, the wife should follow.

Another female student: Teacher, if the husband is a postman, should the wife follow him too, running around all day?

After Participating in the "Welcome Western Kang Compatriots" Meeting 128

Juan Jiu

Recently, the news that has attracted the most attention is the arrival of the Western Kang student delegation in Shanghai. On the 18th of the month, seven organizations in Shanghai jointly held a welcome meeting. During the meeting, formalities were followed. Zheng Tonghe, the principal of Shanghai Middle School, presided over the meeting and delivered a welcome speech, which was divided into three points: (1) Since the founding of the Republic, there have been repeated wars, and unification has not been achieved. Therefore, successive governments have failed to pay attention to border affairs. Now that the national government is unified, it is planning and designing. The Western Kang class that has been trained has graduated. From now on, there will be people to transform Western Kang. (2) Western Kang is located on the border, and transportation is lagging behind. People in the country initially do not know its customs and habits. For example, the book "Strange Tales of Western Travels" mostly insults women in the Sichuan border region. Now, please let the people of Western Kang explain the truth to dispel doubts. (3) Western Kang is located next to Yunnan in the past, and then Qinghai, Tibet to the left, and Sichuan to the right. It has a close relationship with the whole country, but everything remains silent and in ruins as before. Now that these students have come out, Kang affairs may be promising. Next, Pan Yangyao, the representative of the China Vocational Education Society's Border Promotion Association, delivered a speech, also with three other points of significance, carrying the strong color of expanding vocational guidance education to the border areas in the welcome. Then, Sheng Cheng, who had successfully studied in Europe for ten years on a work-study program, gave a speech on the evolution of pastoral life and residential life, and the importance of our nation restoring pastoral life. Mr. Sheng spoke with the demeanor of a professor, unpredictable attitude, and lively tone, earning a lot of applause. Next, Tian Huijin, a professor at Northeastern University, recounted the general situation of municipal administration in various European and American countries. At this point, the Shanghai Middle School harmonica team played, refreshing the audience's nerves. Then, Lu Shunong, the instructor of the delegation, gave a reply.

Ice Fish Revival Method 129

·Ji· Jin

In the bitter cold of winter, ice fish are sometimes found in the market. They do not eat or move, and are almost dead. If you cut them open and look, their hearts are still beating and their blood is fresh and not clotted. In fact, they have not died. My friend Mr. Li, who is a researcher in physics, first uses boiled and cooled water for the experiment. Slightly effervescent, he puts it in a container and adds a small amount of ice. After waiting for the temperature to gradually decrease, he then puts the fish in. After some time, it completely freezes. The fish is still motionless. Then he increases the temperature or exposes it to sunlight. The thick ice gradually melts after several days. When it has melted to a certain degree, the fish gradually returns to its original state and can swim freely. According to him, any frozen fish, even if it has been frozen for half a month, can still be revived. The most important thing is that when water turns into ice and ice turns into water, the rate of change in temperature should not be too rapid. The fish's ability to revive depends entirely on this slow effect. These are his words, and I would like to ask wise physicists for their comments.

He also reported on the educational policy of the class and the implementation of the past. Then, Yang Zhonghua, a student representative of the delegation, reported on the political, educational, industrial, and commercial conditions in Western Kang, as well as the monetary system and other situations, and the process of coming to study. He also mentioned a Western Kang folk tale of a mixed-race father with five sons, to symbolize that the five races should unite and unite to save the country, and that they had suffered from the explicit and implicit oppression of various imperialists in the past. Now that they have come south, it is like a little brother coming to find an older brother, saying, "Older brother, the foreign devils are beating me." His voice and expression were tragic, making people feel both emotional and excited, both sad and happy. Next, He Lixi, a female student from the delegation who was fifteen or sixteen years old, reported on the past and present lives of women in Western Kang, and that she and her friend Bo Zhixi would return to Kang in the future to start with education and awaken women in Western Kang as their vocation. The lady has lived in Peiping for a long time, is lively in demeanor, and speaks Mandarin very fluently. Her speech was also concise and to the point. Finally, five or six of the male students of the group performed Kang dance and Tibetan music, including (Knowing Sound Song) Zangye Quzha Jiacuo by the ancient musician Quzha Jiacuo, and (Social Dance) A Ma Le Si, (God of Flowers) Bai Mei Baiduo, and (Welcome Song) La Da Xi Bei, etc. First, two people stood shoulder to shoulder and hugged each other, advancing and retreating, and touching their left feet back and forth as if kissing. Later, many people stood apart, rotating and advancing and retreating left and right, corresponding to the singing. As for the tunes, they were strangely harsh. As for the lyrics, they were twisted and difficult, and the listeners did not understand them.

Reminiscences of Mr. Chu Minyi's Words 130

Ai Lun

Some time ago, the Chinese Harmonica Association held a tea party for members at the Hua An Building on the eighth floor. Over a hundred people attended. In addition to the fun and entertainment, there were also speeches by Mr. Cai Yuanpei, Chu Minyi, and Chen Heqin. Because Mr. Chu's topic was "Music and Physical Education," he spoke in great detail. Because Mr. Chu was a hygienist and a physical educator, he was able to explain everything thoroughly. Now, I will record the main points to inform those who study music and physical education. Mr. Chu said that the harmonica is the best instrument in music. It is cheap, easy to learn, and convenient, unlike Western instruments, which cost dozens or hundreds of yuan and take several years to master. As for the role of music in life, it has been with us since birth. A newborn can cry, which is its music and its physical education, because crying can expand the lungs. Mothers often see their babies crying and feed them with milk, which is actually a very unhealthy practice and should be strictly avoided. Also, there is a world of difference between the physique of Chinese and Western performers. Famous European and American performers know a lot about hygiene, so their dantian is full and their voices are loud. They can be on stage for a very long time, without any fatigue from beginning to end. On the other hand, Chinese famous performers often have bad habits, their bodies are weak, their voices are low, and they are accompanied by very loud instruments, and the time is short, which cannot create an orderly atmosphere for the audience. Although Chinese and Western dramas are different in nature and structure, the strength of the performers' bodies is very important. Therefore, studying music also requires attention to physical education. Chinese singing emphasizes the dantian, and Tai Chi also emphasizes the dantian. The dantian seems to be the diaphragm. In order to make the lungs move, it is necessary to expand not only to the left and right, but also up and down. These are all physical education issues. Now, if we hold a harmonica and blow it slowly in the morning and evening, it is enough to easily expand the lungs, and it may be an aid to physical education, not just entertainment.

Proverbs About Sheep 131

Qiu Lang

A few days ago, I read "Xin Wei New Dictionary" by Mei Hua Guan Zhu, which was very interesting. I couldn't help but feel itchy and wrote a few sheep proverbs to amuse myself.

Good luck and prosperity is a common saying. According to the ancient meaning of the character 羊 (sheep), it means auspiciousness.

"Sheep's foot bones" is a Hangzhou dialect term for firewood that is small and flimsy. Calling it "sheep's foot bones" is to imply that it is not enough to be used as fuel.

Lamb and fine wine are both excellent products. This means that there are delicacies and mellow wine, just right for light drinking and low conversation.

"A sheep falls into a tiger's mouth" This metaphor refers to the weak encountering the strong and violent, like a sheep falling into a tiger's mouth, with no escape.

"Learning three parts of sheep epilepsy" There is a folk saying that learning three parts of sheep epilepsy is good enough to earn a living.

"Selling lamb as dog meat" This refers to someone who urgently wants to sell goods for money and sells them at a low price.

"Getting a body full of sheep stench" Those who are caught in a whirlpool or want to seek benefits but end up with no real benefit often say, "I didn't eat the lamb, but I got a body full of stench."

"The wool comes from the sheep's body" This means that the cost of goods is high, and the selling price will naturally increase accordingly.

Strange News About Wax Figures Playing Chess 132

Bi Ren

In modern times, science is flourishing, and wise people do not talk about magical things. If the following were discovered in a time when science was not clear, cunning people would use it as a rare commodity to deceive ignorant villagers. This kind of art is an optical effect, and is based on the same principle as mirages, but it is only the difference between natural and man-made, and it is not worth mentioning. The other day, my friend returned from Paris. We were chatting at his hotel when he happened to mention a strange event in Paris. He said that there was a Go club where players had to bet money to play, but they always lost. The chess master was made of wax, and his face, hands, and feet were no different from a living person. The owner of the club first disassembled the wax figure to show the guests that there was nothing inside its hollow abdomen. When playing chess, when the guest made a move, the wax figure also made a move. The result was that the guest always lost and the wax figure won. It was strange enough that the wax figure could play chess, but it was even stranger that it never lost. Later, someone found out the secret. It was said that several chess masters were gathered upstairs in the club. Many mirrors were hung next to the chessboard, which could reflect light to the upstairs. The chess masters upstairs could see every move the guests made. They then used electricity to move the wax figure. So it was not the wax figure that was winning, but the chess masters. That was why it was invincible. Many people who heard about it were curious and flocked to it. The owner of the club made a fortune.

Rambling Notes from the Shanghai Bund 133

Song Lu

I have returned to Shanghai. Several months have passed again. Old friends are scattered, and the world is full of changes. Quietly observing the ten-mile foreign concessions, the prosperity is even more different than before, and the novelty of things is also progressing with each year. I dip my brush to record these impressions, as a way to express my feelings.

If you want to know the development of material civilization, you only need to look at the transportation. When I first arrived in Shanghai, I had a lot of luggage. So, I ordered my servant to hail a yellow car to carry it. Upon arriving at the destination, I asked the price. One yuan was enough. Stable, fast, and cheap, nothing could surpass it. From this one aspect alone, one can see the convenience of transportation in Shanghai. Material prosperity has its origins.

Reading the newspaper, I was surprised to see the so-called First Credit Insurance Company. I was astonished by the novelty of its business. So, I asked for its details. It is also like other insurance businesses that charge annual fees. But the premium is particularly high, requiring 2% of the annual value (i.e., an insurance of 10,000 yuan requires a prepaid premium of 200 yuan). Nowadays, there are too many people and too few jobs in Shanghai, and finding insurance is indeed as difficult as the company described. However, if an employee with an annual income of 400 yuan must guarantee an amount of 10,000 yuan, then half of their annual salary would be used to pay the insurance premium.

Tired of reading, I took a nap. Suddenly, I was awakened by a shouting sound. Listening to it, it seemed to be someone collecting dregs from opium pipe heads. I was curious about the name. Asking a colleague, he said, "It is the water residue from boiling opium paste." I asked what it was used for. He said it would be used to feed the opium addicts. Alas, making a living in Shanghai is truly unimaginable.

Huang Cuojiu, a prominent figure in Shanghai, has passed away. Huang's merits and demerits in life will have their own evaluation. I will not repeat them here. However, Huang loved scholars and was eager for talent throughout his life, which is especially commendable today. As far as I know, people such as Shushisheng of Shanghai, Shannong of Tiantai Mountain, Qizishanren, Yingchuan Qiushui, Xu Tianma, and Wu Yu Gong Xu Hangsu, all had the friendship of guests with Huang. Sun Yusheng and Liu Shannong were especially respected by Huang. Huang was originally just an ordinary merchant. Looking at his life, the only things he relied on to achieve great success were his ability to observe the times and recognize people. Huang was generous, valued integrity, and liked to help people in need. Whenever someone asked for something, he always readily agreed. His good deeds were also commendable.

News from the silver screen: Since the popularity of sound films, most of the major cinemas in Shanghai have switched to showing sound films. Only the Paris Cinema on Avenue Joffre, which specializes in showing first-class silent films, can still stand out. Last Sunday, the cinema held a trial screening of "Reckless" starring Greta Garbo, inviting more than a hundred members of the press. From beginning to end, the film is not only known for its romance and glamour, but Garbo is also able to fully express the pain of a second love. When she wants to leave but also wants to stay, her expression, which is neither crying nor laughing, is even more moving. As for the elegance of the background and the uniformity of the supporting actors, these are just secondary matters. It is heard that the film has been officially released in the cinema since the 21st. (Sheng Pu)

Parisian Tales (X) (II) 134

Liu Ceng, residing in Paris

(II) Donogoo

Among the new plays recently staged in Paris this year, the one that has attracted the most attention and discussion from theater critics is "Donogoo," a recent work by Jules Romains.

Romains is currently a first-class poet and playwright in France. He specializes in studying the complex collective psychology of the "Unanimist School" (Ecole unanime). He has also written several novels, such as "The Death of Someone" (La mort de quelqu'un) and "Lucienne," which are very famous. However, his most beneficial success in the literary world is his play "Knock" (Knock Le Trlomphe de la medesineo). "Knock" is a comedy that specializes in satirizing doctors. He exposes the insidious tricks of many modern unscrupulous doctors who use the beautiful name of science to scare the public, turning healthy people into sick ones. His attitude of challenging doctors is simply in line with the great French 17th-century comedy writer Moliere. However, his satire is even more venomous than Moliere's. Although "Knock" was fiercely opposed by medical associations in various places after its premiere, the general audience praised it extraordinarily. The box office success was rare in the last decade.

This "Donogoo," which premiered this year, cannot be entirely considered a new work. Ten years ago, Romains used this theme to write a screenplay published in Nouvelle Revue Francaise. This time, it was just changed into a stage play. But a few months ago, when news and theater advertisements revealed that "Donogoo" would be rehearsed at the Pigalle Theater (Theatre Pigalle), those who were fond of drama were already looking forward to it, treating it as a rare piece of news, as a major change in the theatrical world. Why is this? One reason is that Romains has a great reputation. Second, although the recently renovated organ stage of the Pigalle Theater, where "Donogoo" is rehearsed, cannot be said to be the best in the world, it can at least be considered the newest and largest in Paris. Third, the premiere of "Donogoo" can give a glimpse of whether stage drama will eventually be eliminated by film.

Cotton Market Soars Seven Cents 141

The cotton market's upward trend is becoming increasingly intense. The continuous rise in American cotton prices and the prospect of further increases have boosted confidence, drawing eager buyers. Many short sellers, recognizing the unfavorable environment, are forced to cover their positions, and large purchases by gold dealers have further tightened the market. Cotton trading is currently active, and market sentiment is noticeably buoyant.

Hanbiao Extremely Buoyant. The Hanbiao market opened with American cotton prices continuing to rise, resulting in strong buying interest. Prices increased by two to three cents in early trading, and the tight market conditions led to further gains of five to six cents in the second and third sessions. The upward momentum persisted into the afternoon, with prices rising another five fen to two cents. Total daily trading volume reached 155,600 bales. Grain and Rice Market Continues Downward Trend 143

Zhabei. Yesterday, arrivals at various wharves were substantial, reaching around 80 vessels. Current river inventory is approximately 230 vessels. Sales remain sluggish. Special Grade White Keng rice is still offered at 13.9 yuan, but ordinary rice is priced around 13 yuan. The market sentiment is weak. Sales of thin Indica rice are also slow, with prices falling by nearly a dime. Premium Grade Yangxian rice is still offered at 12.7-12.8 yuan, with limited retail interest and no significant market activity. The price of Du Bu jian tong rice is stable, while inferior grades are struggling at various yuan levels, with sales matching. The situation is considered stable.

South Shanghai. Yesterday, 30 vessels arrived at the riverbank. Sales were slow. Changshu and Beikeng rice prices are continuing to decline, with the top price at 13 yuan. Suzhou and Tongji Keng rice buying interest is also quiet, and sales are not expanding. Transactions are limited, and various Keng rice prices are down by one or two dimes. Baiyuan rice remains mediocre, and alcohol sales are stagnant, similar to the previous day.

Flour Prices Slightly Firmer in the Evening Market 144

Yesterday's flour market opened weak in the morning for all months. The lowest price for the current month reached 2.095 taels. However, as factories were largely taking a wait-and-see approach and external selling pressure did not intensify, the market stabilized. In the afternoon session, the gold price rose again, naturally causing foreign exchange rates to decline. Selling pressure was therefore minimal. Many speculative short positions were also covered, seemingly stabilizing the market. Given the current circumstances, the spot price for the current month is not strong (military supply spot prices need 2.175 taels), so a significant price decline seems unlikely. However, if the factories also have excess flour, the ultimate downward pressure will come from this factor. As a result, the current month fell slightly by 0.005 taels compared to the previous day, February rose by 0.0075 taels, March rose by 0.01 taels, April rose by 0.0075 taels, May rose by 0.01 taels, and June rose by 0.005 taels.

Forward Wheat Tends to Weaken 145

Yesterday's wheat futures market showed a generally flat to weak trend for all months in both the morning and afternoon sessions. With delivery of the current month approaching, both longs and shorts are gradually liquidating positions. The trading volume on the exchange was still over 200 cars, but the actual delivery will probably be within 100 cars, and a portion has already been settled bilaterally beforehand. Therefore, there are no major issues overall. For the far-month contracts, foreign quotations only showed slight fluctuations, and the amount of margin on the exchange was steadily dumped by market participants, causing market sentiment to be difficult to boost. As a result, the current month was up 0.01 taels from the previous day, February was down 0.01, March was down 0.01, April was down 0.01, May was down 0.02, and June was down 0.03 taels. Spot wheat is still unquoted due to limited arrivals and sales.

Huang Shaoxiong and Wife Arrive in Shanghai from Hong Kong Yesterday Morning 152

Ma Xiaojun and Wu Tingyang Arrive Together

Chen Shi Proceeds to Beijing Yesterday Afternoon

Huang and Others to Rest Briefly in Shanghai

Huang Shaoxiong, former Chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government, and his wife arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 8:00 am aboard the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's Shinyo Maru from Hong Kong. Accompanying them were Wu Tingyang, former Director of the Guangxi Provincial Government's Department of Construction, Ma Xiaojun, Chief Counselor of the General Headquarters, Chen Shi, Counselor, and Gong Jieyuan, a total of six people. The Shinyo Maru was originally scheduled to arrive in port on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, but due to fog, it was anchored in the Tongsha waters, delaying its arrival at the Wusong Estuary until 6:00 am yesterday and reaching Shanghai at 8:00 am. It docked at the Huishan Wharf at 8:20 am. Welcoming them at the port were Deng Jiayan, former Secretary-General of the Eighth Route Army, and dozens of Huang's family members and friends.

Meeting with Reporters. After the ship docked, welcomers and reporters from various newspapers boarded the ship to pay their respects. Mr. Huang, dressed in a black suit, was energetic and came out to meet them personally, shaking hands with each welcomer. He then met with reporters from various newspapers in the reception room, introduced by Deng Jiayan. Mr. Huang answered the reporters' questions in detail, speaking for about fifteen minutes before the reporters took their leave.

Mission to Beijing. Mr. Huang said, "I am here on the orders of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to report on the details of Guangxi Province. There are areas where the Central Government is unclear about the situation in Guangxi, and I can explain them in person. The Central Government will decide on the follow-up issues in Guangxi, and I have no objections. The war in Guangxi has long since ended. The Guangdong Army is stationed on the front lines in Guizhou, Guilin, and Guixian. Water and land transportation between Guangdong and Guangxi provinces has not yet been restored. Li, Bai, Zhang, and others are still in Guangxi, but their movements are uncertain."

Yunnan Army Withdraws. Huang Wen said, "Li Mingrui, Yu Zuoyu, Wei Baqun, and other units colluded with the communists and acted rampantly, repeatedly disturbing Longzhou and Baise. They have now fled to Jingzhou on the Hunan border and the Pingshi and Lanyang areas of Guangdong. The majority of the Yunnan Army has returned to Kunming, with only a small portion stationed on the Guangxi border."

Departure from Vietnam. "I left Liuzhou on November 24. Due to transportation difficulties, it took me about a month to reach Longzhou. I originally planned to pass through Vietnam to Hong Kong and then Shanghai, but at that time, the French authorities, citing the burning of the French Consulate in Longzhou by Li Mingrui's troops, prohibited Guangxi people from crossing the border, causing me to be stranded in Longzhou for a month. On the 13th of this month, I finally passed through Vietnam to Hong Kong. In Hong Kong, I met Mr. Ma Xiaojun and others, and we came to Shanghai together. Reports that I went to Guangzhou are incorrect. I now plan to rest in Shanghai for a few days before going to Beijing to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek."

Ma Xiaojun's Remarks. Our reporter specifically interviewed Mr. Ma Xiaojun, the Chief Counselor of the General Headquarters, who accompanied Huang to Shanghai. Mr. Ma said, "I was ordered to go to Guangxi to engage in peace work. Fortunately, Li, Bai, Zhang, and others have realized the situation, stopped fighting, and are awaiting the Central Government to handle the aftermath. Regarding the follow-up issues in Guangxi, generally, Li and Bai will step down and go abroad, the army will be reorganized, the Central Government will send personnel to preside over Guangxi's administration, and the guest troops in Guangxi will be relocated to other defense areas by the Central Government. After Mr. Huang enters Beijing and meets with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, detailed measures will be determined. Zhang Fakui's troops now number only a few thousand, and their attitude is entirely based on the attitude of Li and Bai."

Chen Shi Goes to Beijing. Mr. Ma said, "Mr. Huang will be staying in Shanghai for several days. Counselor Chen Shi of the General Headquarters was recently ordered to go to Guangdong. He accompanied us to Shanghai and has taken the express train to Beijing this afternoon (i.e., yesterday) to report everything to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in advance. In a few days, I will accompany Mr. Huang to Beijing."

Citywide Industry Associations Gather to Discuss Tax Issues 153

Establishment of Tax Research Committee

The city's various industry associations held a general meeting of industry representatives yesterday afternoon at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce auditorium to discuss the issue of tax increases after the abolition of Likin, which is of great importance to industry and commerce. Over a hundred organizations, including the Money Trade Association, Tobacco Factory Association, Cotton Cloth Association, Silk Association, Medicine Association, New Medicine Association, Dried Goods Association, Wood Industry Association, Knitting Association, and others, sent over 160 representatives, including Luo Qinghua, Zheng Chengqing, Hu Xisheng, Jiang Zhigang, Shen Weiting, Chen Feiyuan, and Zhu Wenqi. Zheng Chengqing was elected chairman. After performing the ceremonial rituals, the chairman reported, "Distinguished representatives, today we have gathered representatives from various industries specifically to discuss the issue of tax increases after the abolition of Likin. We know that the quality of taxes is closely related to the prosperity and decline of industry and commerce. The Likin system of the past eighty years has directly bankrupted Chinese industry and commerce. This is the impact of poor tax policies. Now that the government is abolishing Likin, if the compensatory taxes are inappropriate, they will burden merchants and cripple industry. Moreover, the General Outline of Business Tax in various provinces stipulates that the members of the Business Tax Review Committee will be composed of tax officials, representatives of chambers of commerce, and designated accountants. We should not forget the position of commercial organizations and contribute as much as possible to the financial authorities for adoption. The Business Tax Collection Regulations promulgated by Zhejiang Province exceed the General Outline of Business Tax by a significant amount. Our city is adjacent to Zhejiang, with some companies having their headquarters in Shanghai and branches in Zhejiang, and others having their headquarters in Zhejiang and branches in Shanghai. The interests are closely intertwined. Furthermore, Zhejiang's promulgation of Business Tax Regulations is the first among the provinces, and in the future, other provinces will follow Zhejiang's lead. The impact will be significant. Do not disregard the matter simply because it pertains to Zhejiang. It should be known that Likin has caused harm for eighty years, spreading its poison throughout the country, starting with just the Xiannv Temple in Yangzhou. Therefore, at today's meeting, we should strive to address the excessive regulations on business tax in Zhejiang, and request that the Shanghai Municipal Government lightly tax industry and commerce, and ensure equal treatment for Chinese and foreign businesses in the Chinese and foreign concessions. It is hoped that the representatives present will express their opinions as much as possible, so that the most comprehensive solutions can be offered to the government authorities." After the chairman's report, discussions began, and the following results were achieved: (1) A telegram will be sent to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting a reduction in the business tax rate. (2) A petition will be submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government requesting that Chinese and foreign businesses in the Chinese and foreign concessions receive equal treatment when drafting the General Outline of Business Tax, and that industry representatives be allowed to participate in discussions. (3) A Tax Research Committee consisting of industry associations will be established, and the following members will be appointed: Zheng Chengqing, Zhu Wenqi, Luo Qinghua, Zheng Meiluo, Ge Liangqing, Mao Chunpu, Shen Weiting, Sun Choucheng, Ye Chunqiao, Yu Baoxing, Wang Lianfang, Jiang Zhigang, Xie Zhongle, Lin Zhangrong, and Cheng Youfu, totaling fifteen people. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions.

British Economic Mission Hosts Reception for All Sectors Last Night 154

Thomson's Farewell Speech

The British Far East Economic Mission is scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 27th of this month for Guangdong, first to Hong Kong and then to Guangzhou, to inspect for one month, and then return to their country via Canada, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. As their departure is imminent, the Mission held a grand banquet at the Cathay Hotel last night to thank all sectors. Those present included Navy Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan, Jiangsu Higher Court Second Branch President Xu Weizhen, American Assessor Pandi, British Consul General Bai Linan, Industry Ministry's Shanghai Visiting Bureau Director Zhao Jinqing, Shanghai Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Industry Ministry Secretary Xu Jianping, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce President Wang Xiaolai, Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Director Zou Bingwen, Zhejiang Industrial Bank President Xu Xinliu, Bank of China President Zhang Jia'ao, Zhejiang Industrial Bank President Li Ming, Central Mint Director Guo Biao, Foreign Affairs Office Shanghai Deputy Director Liu Yunfang, Fuxin Flour Mill General Manager Rong Zongjing, McLaren College President Xia Jinlin, Japanese Textile Industry Council Chairman Funatsu, British Chamber of Commerce President Marshall, Shen Bao's Gu Angruo, Xinwen Bao's Gu Zhizhong, North China Daily News's Semussen, Reuters's Gugges, and 200 others. The banquet was presided over by Sir Thomson, head of the British Economic Mission. The Cathay Hotel's music accompanied the dinner. After the banquet, Sir Thomson gave a speech thanking all sectors for their warm hospitality. Chen Shaokuan and Pandi also gave speeches on behalf of the guests. The gathering ended on a joyful note late into the night.

Thomson said in his speech, "British Consul General in Beijing, Sir Schneider, has received a special award from the national government, and we are delighted to have him here today. We have received warm hospitality in China, which has greatly comforted our mission. We would also like to thank all sectors for providing us with valuable assistance and helpful information. We have been in China for over four months, investigating and reporting on how to improve British trade. The decline of British-China commerce is well known. During our short time here, you expect me to tell you our impressions. However, this is difficult because there is so much we have seen and so much we have learned. We must sit down and organize it to obtain a true picture of all the issues surrounding trade between our countries. I think we have an understanding of what has happened in China, which has dramatically changed the situation. We must acknowledge these changes and prepare to move forward on a path of progress. People back home must work with the various industries here to meet the trends. Domestic exporters must have closer cooperation with importers here. If all parties approach it with determination and cooperation, everything can be hoped for. Our deepest impression is that China needs peace. We all agree that the establishment of lasting peace is sufficient to obtain stability and security, not only to make all industries flourish, but also to generally progress national social causes. China's foreign trade only reaches 12% of its population and only accounts for 2% of the world's total foreign trade, so there is room to increase its commercial position. This is not only our expectation but something that can be achieved. A peaceful China will greatly increase its trade capacity, import, and export business, and the UK hopes to occupy an important position in this. As for us, we will provide manufacturers and merchants at home with the facts and reports we have obtained to help them achieve this goal. The stability and security of China will attract financial assistance, which is essential during its construction period. Regarding this point, I firmly believe that the UK can participate. When the Blackburn Chamber of Commerce sent a mission in 1896, the price of silver in Shanghai was 2 shillings 11 pence per tael in November 1896, and it fell to 2 shillings 3.5 pence in September 1897, causing the entire business to plummet. When we arrived in Shanghai on October 25, the price of silver was 1 shilling 7 pence per tael, and today it has fallen to 1 shilling 3 pence. We are very concerned about the current price of silver and its impact on China's exchange rate. We cannot make any decisions for a while, but I feel that the world cannot allow it to hinder the restoration and prosperity of business. We deeply feel that there are many things China can do to adopt British engineering, such as electricity, sanitation, and running water, to improve the comfort of life and promote transportation to promote workers' abilities and improve the standard of living. We have also carefully and closely investigated important cotton and wool weaving industries. The results are difficult to say at the moment. However, we must let British manufacturers obtain the true situation of the Far East market. As for the cotton weaving industry, the UK will never fall behind.

Based on the results of our investigation in the East, we dare to say that the equipment of the Lancashire yarn factories is the best in the world, and their products are sufficient to meet the needs of the world market. Our mission is very optimistic, but to remedy the market and restore the original commerce, the public must have absolute self-confidence. Not only Shanghai is like this, but the whole world is like this. What has been lost in the past, we often lack self-confidence, and look forward without moving forward. From now on, if we can fight bravely and resolutely to overcome negative ideas, then the victory in the future will be assured. China's greatest need at the moment is peace and unity. It is hoped that the National Government's construction work will flourish. British merchants around the world will work together, and the UK's position in world commerce can be maintained. I raise this glass to wish the two countries of China and the UK boundless prosperity.

Public Concession Patrol's Plan for Preventing Kidnapping 155

Approved by the Board of Directors

To be Implemented Gradually Within Days

For the purpose of preventing kidnapping and protecting residents, the Public Concession Patrol has drafted a plan to increase police force and facilitate arrests. It has now been approved by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department and will be implemented gradually within days. The content is roughly as follows: (1) Install roadside telephones; (2) Install wireless telephones in police stations and patrol cars so that communication can be maintained at all times; (3) Increase the number of patrol cars and motorcycles; (4) Organize special plainclothes teams; (5) Find suitable housing in the western district of the concession to set up a reserve patrol team. The total start-up cost for all items is approximately 118,000 taels, and the annual recurring cost will increase by approximately 56,000 taels. Regarding the installation of roadside telephones, the police station has been considering it for some time. Recently, the Shanghai Telephone Company's draft proposal has been adopted by the police department. Once an order is placed with the company, it can be installed in approximately nine months. After that, patrol officers and detectives can communicate with the police station at any time and place. In the event of an incident, patrol officers and detectives can immediately report to the police station, and the police station can also direct detectives at any time. Residents can also report to the police station immediately through patrol officers and detectives. In addition, it is planned to add wireless telephone sets to major police stations and install headphones in each patrol car to transmit orders. If there is a theft alarm in one place, nearby vehicles can be summoned to arrest the perpetrators. These patrol cars will usually patrol in sections to carry out search work, inspect passing vehicles, and supplement with motorcycles to patrol the alleys. In addition, automobile teams will be stationed at the main intersections in the western district, where serious kidnapping cases often occur, to conduct regular inspections. According to the minimum calculation, this patrol fleet requires approximately twelve cars and sixteen motorcycles to be dispatched. If suitable housing can be found in the western district, a reserve patrol team will be added to assist the inspection teams stationed at various main intersections. According to the police station's opinion, after this plan is fully implemented, it will be more effective in preventing kidnapping cases, so that Chinese residents can feel safer and trust the police station's capabilities more, and hope that they can support the police station more, cooperate with each other, eliminate violence, and ensure the safety of the community.

Higher Branch Court Handles Shanghai Political Prisoner Amnesty Case 158

Totaling More Than Ten Political Prisoners

Transferred to the Jiangsu Higher Court for Review

Release Can Be Expected Next Week

The National Government's amnesty for political prisoners on New Year's Day of the 20th year of the Republic of China, after the decree was announced, and the procedures and methods for amnesty were stipulated, were handled by the Higher Courts of each province organizing review committees. Therefore, in the past ten days, the Higher Courts of each province have been actively handling this matter. In Shanghai, because there are more cases and the relationships are also more important, how the Shanghai Higher Branch Court is handling the situation has attracted much attention. A reporter from this newspaper made a special visit to the Higher Branch Court yesterday. According to the news from the procuratorate, the National Government's amnesty case was originally stipulated by the Ministry of Justice to be handled by the Higher Court, and the branch court could not handle it on its behalf. Later, the Hebei Higher Branch Court submitted a request to the Ministry of Justice for interpretation. The Ministry of Justice then reissued an order requiring the Higher Court to handle it. Although this branch court is directly under the Ministry of Justice, which is different from other branch courts, since the ministry's order has been stipulated, it still follows the ministry's order and does not organize a review committee. Only the political prisoners who have been judged by the former Provisional Court and this branch court (those who have served their terms have of course been released long ago, which is not a problem) who meet the amnesty regulations, totaling about a dozen people (the list must be approved before it can be published), are compiled and sent to the procuratorate of this branch court. This procuratorate will then forward it to the review committee of the Suzhou Higher Court. After the committee approves it, they can be released. This list has now been completed and is planned to be sent out today or tomorrow. It is expected to be replied to next week.

Piloted by B.R. Phillipe to Little Luzon

The US Maclain Co.'s Phoenix aircraft departed from Hongqiao Airport at 8:10 yesterday morning, flying to Little Luzon. The pilot was Mr. B.R. Phillipe. Mrs. Phillipe originally planned to fly with her husband, but because the cabin was loaded with gasoline, taking up a lot of space, it did not materialize. After proceeding for about 1,500 feet, the plane went straight into the clouds. The speed of the plane is 105 miles per hour, so it can reach Guangzhou in nine hours at the latest.

Special Tax Issues on Silk and Cocoons 160

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Inquires with the Ministry of Finance

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, it is reported that, according to a report on the 17th, the Special Tax Preparatory Office of the Ministry of Finance stipulated that the scope of collection of taxes on silkworms originally included the joint collection of cocoons, silk, and silk fabrics. The current tax rules

Page 14

The association believes that the joint collection of three items is similar to double taxation, and it has been decided to exempt silk and only collect taxes on cocoons and silk fabrics, etc. According to Article 4 of the Special Consumption Tax Regulations passed by the five-province tax reduction conference on December 5th of the 17th year of the Republic of China and promulgated by your ministry, it is stipulated that when the goods listed in this regulation are subject to heavy taxes, the original taxes shall be refunded separately according to the nature of the goods. The methods are as follows: (1) When collecting silkworm silk tax, refund the cocoon tax; (2) When collecting silk fabric tax, refund the silkworm silk tax, etc. The regulations are extremely detailed. With the tax refund system, there is no need to worry about the so-called heavy tax situation. If, as the original telegram says, instead of using tax refunds as a means to avoid heavy taxes, only collecting taxes on cocoons and silk fabrics is used as a way to avoid double taxation, then is it not a duplication to pay cocoon tax and then silk fabric tax? Moreover, in fact, only when cocoons and silk are woven into silk fabrics can they be consumed by people. Therefore, the consumption tax systems of various countries mostly tax finished products and not raw materials. We believe that the person who sent this telegram has not only not explored the tax rules, but also seems to be unaware of the consumption tax regulations promulgated by the ministry, which has led to this speculation. Our association has never dared to regard it as a precedent. However, the silk industry has been worried about this news, fearing that the principle of one item, one tax will be shaken by this. In order to comfort the merchants, we dare not be reckless and telegraph to your ministry, asking you to investigate the truth and reassure the public, which is convenient for everyone. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows."

Request to Allow Unregistered Private School Students to Take Entrance Exams 164

Various Universities Petition the Ministry of Education

The Ministry of Education's crackdown on substandard private schools is very strict. Therefore, graduates and students of unregistered private schools cannot be treated the same as graduates or students of national or registered public and private schools, and are not allowed to transfer to national or registered schools to study. However, in order to help students from unregistered schools in this city with their studies, the universities in this port have repeatedly held meetings to discuss in detail that while substandard schools should be strictly cracked down on, the responsibility does not lie with the students, and that there are many outstanding people among the unregistered schools. If they are not helped, good and bad will be destroyed together, which is unfair and not the way for the country to cultivate talents. Therefore, they unanimously advocated jointly petitioning the Ministry of Education to change the method and allow national or registered schools to strictly examine and enroll students from unregistered private schools. It is reported that the documents were prepared the day before yesterday and submitted to the Ministry of Education for review. The original text of the submission to the ministry is as follows: "Respectfully submitted, recently read in the newspaper that your ministry is reviewing the qualifications of new students and transfer students reported by public and private universities this year, and all students from unregistered private schools have been ordered to withdraw from school. It shows your ministry's intention to strictly crack down on private schools. However, the schools, etc., believe that private schools that do not comply with the order to register and whose management does not meet the requirements can be ordered to close down to avoid misleading young people. As for the students who are studying and have graduated from schools such as Liao School, not all of them are stubborn and cannot be cultivated. If they are all given the punishment of withdrawing from school, there is a risk of destroying both good and bad. Moreover, before your ministry issued a clear order to crack down on private schools, these students did not know that they were making a mistake when they entered the school, and there are also many outstanding people among them. Now, if they are all prohibited from transferring or continuing their studies, then these students' years of time and money will be wasted, and the path to further education will be cut off from now on, which is a pity. Although your ministry had a screening test for students from private schools last summer, the time for the notice was short and it was only held in Shanghai. There may be places in remote areas of the interior that are not fully aware of it, or they may not have been able to take the exam as scheduled due to inconvenient transportation, so most students still feel regret and have no choice but to directly take the entrance exams of various schools. Although their level is comparable and they have been admitted, they are still subject to the punishment of withdrawal due to their qualifications. The spring enrollment period this year is approaching again, and most students from private schools are wandering on different paths, in a dilemma, which is pitiful. The schools, etc., have witnessed the situation and dare not remain silent. Therefore, they jointly petition your ministry to change the handling method. Before the deadline for private schools to register in the ministry's order this year, when students studying or graduating from unregistered private schools take the entrance exams of various schools, they will be allowed to take strict exams. If they pass, they will be treated the same as students from public or registered schools in order to help them. As for the strict examination method, your ministry can send personnel to supervise the examination, or your ministry can set another method. Is it appropriate? We hope that you will review and instruct us to comply, which is convenient for everyone. Respectfully submitted to the Minister of Education, Jiang, the listed schools include Datong, Fudan, Hujiang, Guanghua, Daxia, Soochow, Political Science, Zhonggong, Law School, etc., a total of nine schools."

Special News from the Shipping Industry 165

Fog Blocks Various Ships from Arriving in Shanghai

The Shanghai area was foggy the day before yesterday, and a total of more than twenty merchant ships from the Yangtze River and the sea were blocked outside Wusongkou. The fog had dissipated by yesterday morning and afternoon, and the ships were able to enter the port one after another. The river ships included Anji, Jiangxin, Jiangshan, Huangpu, Ruiyang, and the sea ships Sichuan, Zhi Shalak, and Xi Hou, all of which were delayed by one day. Yesterday, more than forty ships entered the Huangpu River in one day. The departure dates of the ships were also delayed by one day.

Discussing Escort Issues

The four companies operating on the Shanghai-Ningbo route proposed to establish a security force to escort ships. The four-ship tea room has opposed this, and has submitted a memorandum to the companies, willing to have the crew兼任卫队. This matter concerns maritime safety, and the matter is inevitable. The Sanbei Company yesterday sent a letter to China Merchants Taikoo Ning Shao, inviting them to send representatives to the bureau today to discuss the issue of whether to establish a self-owned guard team or have the crew double as the guard team. The ship will arrive in Shanghai today. After the Xinming ship was stolen, the cargo inside the ship has been investigated by the surveyor Lloyd's. Yesterday, the ship telegraphed the Shanghai Bureau, saying that it has left Min and is heading to Shanghai. However, there are many fruits in Fuzhou that need to be loaded and transported urgently, and the passenger family still ordered the resumption of this route. The Fujian Provincial Garrison Headquarters has sent sixteen guards to the ship to serve as an escort team and protect the ship. The ship can arrive in Shanghai today.

The Water Level of the Upper Yangtze River Declines Sharply

The water level of the Upper Yangtze River has declined sharply in recent days. Vessels of 500 tons cannot navigate between Hankou and Yichang, and the water level in Hunan is even lower. In recent days, a large number of cotton and food have been transported to Shanghai from Hunan. The ships cannot go to load. The six companies in this port have agreed to send barges to Hunan to be towed by small ships to Hankou, and then transfer to ships to go down the river.

Floating Bridge Prohibits Stacking Goods

The Shanghai Municipal Government Public Works Bureau yesterday sent a letter to the various shipping companies, saying, "Respectfully, it is found that stacking goods on the wharf floating bridge is extremely easy to cause danger and hinders traffic. It has long been in the category of being banned. At this time, when the revetment and floating bridge are waiting for repairs, stacking goods on the floating bridge should be strictly prohibited. According to the report of the wharf warehouse management office, recently, there have been occasional coolies stacking heavy goods on the floating bridge connecting the revetment, which is extremely dangerous and prohibits them from listening. If the floating bridge collapses, not only will the goods be damaged, but it will be difficult to avoid endangering lives. Please forward the letter to the various shipping companies to strictly prohibit this in order to maintain safety. In the event of damage, the coolies, etc., should be fully responsible." (Abbreviated below)

All Russian Rented Ships Released

The Soviet Russian Commercial Fleet rented more than thirty Chinese merchant ships last spring to sail to Russia. Now, due to the freezing of the North Bay, the ships cannot travel and have been returned to Shanghai.

Widespread Labor Strike at British American Tobacco's Tin Foil Factory in Pudong 167

Factory Authorities Maintain a Firm Stance

Party and Government Mediation Proves Ineffective

Yesterday, All 8,000 Workers Went on Strike

At the British American Tobacco factory in Pudong, last year at the end of the year, claiming slow business, suddenly dismissed 20 workers from the tin foil factory, causing a factory-wide slowdown. For two months, the dispute has not been resolved. The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau have convened labor and management several times for mediation, but the factory has been insincere in accepting, leading both sides to extremes. The night before last (22nd), the union convened an emergency representative meeting and decided to start a factory-wide slowdown for two hours on the morning of the 23rd. If the factory authorities do not wake up, they will continue the spirit of the 1926 general strike and prepare for a long-term struggle. The details are as follows:

Donations for Relief: Since the tin foil factory labor strike occurred on November 14th of last year, the union, considering the approaching end of the year and the urgent need for relief for the workers, decided through a representative meeting to organize an economic preparatory committee to assist the dismissed workers of the tin foil factory, and submitted a request to the higher authorities for registration. Donations were solicited from all workers in the factory, with representatives contributing 40 cents of small silver per month, workers contributing 20 cents of small silver per month, and staff and supervisors making generous donations. The first donation totaled over 1,000 silver dollars, which were distributed to the workers to help them get through the New Year.

Bonus Issue: At the end of last year, the factory was supposed to issue year-end bonuses to the workers as usual, but the tin foil factory refused to issue them. The union sent representatives Geng Sheng, Chen Peide, Gu Ruofeng, and Xie Peiji to the factory on New Year's Eve to negotiate repeatedly. The factory authorities maintained a firm attitude. From 8 am to 10 pm, the representatives received nothing. Zhu Yuanhui, the captain of the Fourth Squad of the Police, mediated and the factory temporarily paid 500 yuan, distributing 5 yuan to each worker.

Final Mediation: The tin foil factory dispute has been repeatedly mediated by the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau without a satisfactory resolution. On the 15th of this month, the union received a notice from the Social Affairs Bureau to convene labor and management to the bureau for mediation. The union sent Gu Ruofeng and Chen Peiji to comply. The factory was represented by Old Bubble, accompanied by translator Cao Yunxiang. As a result of the negotiations, the union representatives expressed concessions, but the factory representatives were insincere in accepting, resulting in no outcome and the meeting adjourned.

Representative Meeting: Since the storm has been mediated several times by the party and government agencies, but the factory authorities have a firm attitude, and the two sides have gone to extremes, the union convened a temporary emergency representative meeting at 8 pm the day before yesterday. All representatives attended on time. Wu Jiaze, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, attended to provide guidance. Chen Peide was elected chairman, and Sun Xiaoshi was the recorder. Many important cases were resolved: (1) Starting at 7 am tomorrow (i.e., yesterday), all workers will slow down for two hours; (2) Issue a slowdown declaration; (3) Post slogans and publish in newspapers; (4) For workers doing early shifts in each department, the representatives of each department are responsible for notification; (5) If the slowdown tomorrow does not produce results, an emergency representative meeting will be convened that night. All the above cases were unanimously approved, and then the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wu Jiaze, gave guidance and adjourned the meeting.

Slowdown Declaration: Dear fellow workers, we 8,000 workers of the British American Tobacco factory are unfortunate to be born in a country with backward industries. Because of our need for survival, we have to submit to the iron hooves of imperialism, use our own blood and sweat to desperately produce for foreigners, and live like cattle and horses. We ask ourselves, we have not let the factory down in the slightest. However, the British imperialist capitalists, relying on the arrogance of their capital power, unreasonably oppress us, often causing disputes and making our lives unstable. Recently, the factory has been spreading rumors, saying that it will move the Pudong factory into the concession, or that it will reduce the scope of the Pudong factory and lay off a large number of people. We thought that this was just the factory's air pressure and would not become a reality. Unexpectedly, on November 14th of last year, the factory suddenly claimed that business was slow and suddenly announced the dismissal of 20 workers from the tin foil factory, giving each person only two weeks' severance pay. The workers were unwilling to accept the double savings and were forcibly driven out of the factory by the head of the department (Bubble), causing the entire department to be indignant and unanimously slowing down to provide assistance and put forward conditions: (1) All dismissed workers must be reinstated; (2) If they cannot be reinstated, each person will be given six months' severance pay in addition to savings; (3) In the future, when new workers are added to the tin foil factory, the dismissed workers must be given priority employment; (4) Replace the Westerner Bubble who beat the workers; (5) The wages during the slowdown period must be paid by the factory. The above conditions have been repeatedly negotiated by the union, together with the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau, at the factory without success. We know that the dismissal conditions put forward by the workers in that department are the minimum. If we cite the fact that the Pudong Nanyang factory stopped production in the past (one year and one month of dismissal pay, 5% double in addition to savings wages), we feel even more ashamed. Moreover, the factory's demand is greater than the supply, and it is not a slow business. Moving jobs is not comparable to stopping production. Why is it difficult to accept a small condition? The factory completely rejected the minimum demand. We are all cranial round toe square, how different is benevolence and unkindness? However, we have always taken care of the feelings of labor and management and avoided unexpected misfortunes. We have repeatedly tolerated all the more than one hundred workers in that department, and donated and rescued them from the whole. We originally hoped that the factory would finally wake up. Who would have thought that for two months, the party and government agencies would mediate again and again, and the factory's attitude was firm and insincere in accepting. Recently, they have intensified their efforts to renege on the workers' year-end bonuses, and even the lackey Cao Yunxiang has tried to sabotage them in many ways. The workers in that department are already unbearable under this double pressure. All the workers are interdependent and it is even more difficult to sit idly by. Now the representative meeting has decided to slow down for two hours. If the factory does not wake up again, it will continue the spirit of the 1926 general strike and fight to the death with the British imperialist capitalists. Dear compatriots, our hot blood is boiling, our grief is tense. We will prepare 8,000 groups of armed forces and start fighting for our lives. Now we will inform all sectors of the facts of the past and seek public judgment. Especially the revolutionary workers in the tobacco industry, the workers of the British American Tobacco factory under the same oppressed class, hope to give us sympathetic assistance so that we can achieve the final victory in the strict barriers of imperialism and capitalism. (The following is omitted)

Warning to Cao Yunxiang: This association's 8,000 workers are forced under the factory's iron hooves, weeping and groaning, and one word is enough. This time, the factory dismissed 20 workers from the tin foil factory for no reason, causing a factory-wide slowdown. The party and government agencies repeatedly mediated, but the factory was insincere in accepting. So far, the dispute has been prolonged for more than two months, and more than one hundred workers are in extreme pain. All those with blood and energy are filled with resentment. Moreover, Mr.'s past behavior and facts are on record, and this association has warned him on file. Two Railway Bureaus Establish Life Insurance 169

Implemented from February

In order to seek security for the employees of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, the two railway bureaus specially initiated the organization of the Two Railway Employee Life Insurance Association. The intention is that all employees of the railway who die of illness or accidental injury during their service will receive a one-time funeral expense of 300 yuan from the association. However, when serving on the railway, each person must pay an insurance premium of 1 yuan per year, paid in four installments. If employees have urgent needs, they can also apply to the association for a loan with a guarantee, deducted from their salary in installments, but not exceeding twice the monthly salary and half of the existing alimony. All regulations have been formulated and distributed to all stations, and all preparations have been made. It will be officially implemented from February. This move is a blessing for the employees of the railway.

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice: This post office will implement a new system from February 1, 1920, allowing Shanghai merchants to attach unsealed return envelopes or postcards to advertising letters, as long as they are prepared according to the prescribed format. This method can be applied to advertising letters sent to various places within China and the Shanghai delivery area. Cruel Methods of Bandits 174

Not only Robbing Clothes and Belongings

But also Killing the Victims

Zhu Huanzhang, a bill collector from the Dongcheng Automobile Company on Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen, Suzhou, was robbed and killed. On the night of the 19th, Zhu Huanzhang, a native of Suzhou, a bill collector from the Dongcheng Automobile Company on Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen, went out after bathing in the Longquan Bathhouse on Zhejiang Road. When he passed the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Shilu Road, he was surrounded and searched by several short-clothed robbers. More than 100 yuan in cash was taken away. Not content with this, they wanted to strip off his clothes. When Zhu shouted, they shot him with a pistol after robbing his clothes. With a loud bang, Zhu fell to the ground in response. When the robbers ran away, he endured the pain and reported to the nearby police. He was hired to be taken to Renji Hospital. The doctor confirmed that the injury was critical. Although the bullet was removed by surgery, it was difficult to take effect. He died in the hospital the afternoon before yesterday. The police station in charge reported that they had sent police to carry the body to the mortuary on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo, a prosecutor from the Special District Local Court, arrived at the mortuary to investigate. The father of the deceased, Zhu Peiqing, requested to claim the body for coffin burial, and asked to quickly arrest the murderer and punish them. Prosecutor Guo approved his request and ordered Zhu Peiqing to make a guarantee, claim the body for coffin burial, and ordered the police to strictly arrest the murderer and bring them to justice for interrogation.

Little Hope for the Missing Old Man in Zhangyan to Return 176

Bandits Concoct a Scheme to Deceive 200 Yuan

Repeated Contacts with No Trace

Family Members Have Already Completed Funeral Rites

Tang Shaoru, an old man from Zhangyan, Jinshan County, who was 77 years old, left the hospital in Shanghai at 7:45 pm on September 16th of last year and suddenly disappeared on the way. His family members offered a reward to find him, but were cheated by bandits who sent letters and lost 200 yuan, etc., which has been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that the old man has been missing for more than four months since he disappeared. It is now heard that his family members have completed funeral rites because there is still no trace. However, the process is quite tortuous and interesting. A total of eight letters of extortion were received from the bandits. The details are recorded as follows: Tang Lao lives in Zhangyan North Street and runs a Tangtai Ji preserved meat shop. He has a wife and a son. His wife is 50 years old and his son is only 14 years old. Tang is very healthy. In August of last year, he came to Shanghai to discuss business. Unexpectedly, he contracted syphilis and was introduced by a friend to a hospital for treatment. As a result, he was overly depressed and his nerves were confused. On September 16th, when his illness recovered slightly, he left the hospital and suddenly disappeared. His family members searched everywhere and posted rewards in the newspaper, but there was no trace. At the end of September, his family suddenly received a letter stating that Tang Lao was unharmed in Shanghai. It was only necessary to prepare 1,500 silver dollars and place the money in the grass shoes left on the grassland east of Xujiahui Railway Station in West Shanghai. After receiving the money, they would send the person back the next day, etc. His family members knew that he had been kidnapped, so they immediately replied to the letter in the grass shoes, asking to reduce the amount of money and to show evidence first. At the beginning of October, they received another letter from the bandits, stating that they would prepare 400 yuan, pay 200 yuan first, and the remaining 200 yuan would be allowed to be delivered the next day. His family members were eager to return home because they thought that Tang was old, so they immediately prepared 200 yuan and sent someone to place it in the broken shoes next to the coffin in the Beicao Pavilion in Xujiahui. The next day, his family members waited anxiously, but unexpectedly there was no news. They realized that they had been defrauded by the bandits. Later, at the beginning of November, his family members were anxious because he had been missing for two months and his whereabouts were still unknown. Unexpectedly, they suddenly received another letter from the bandits, claiming that the money had been received as scheduled, but because the amount was too small, it was not enough to distribute, so they did not send the person. They asked for 1,000 yuan, etc. His family members suspected that it was a trick and ignored it. Unexpectedly, the bandits still sent a letter every five days and a letter every ten days until the end of December, a total of eight letters. What was said in the letter seemed to be Tang Lao's tone, and he described his history from childhood to adulthood in detail without any deviation. He also wrote down the three characters of his unknown nickname "Tang Bench" and asked friends to help find a way to pity his old age. In the eighth letter, he still only needed 200 yuan to be placed in the original place. Upon receipt, he would immediately send the person back. This small amount was only used to pay for food expenses, etc., because Tang was ill, so as not to end his life, etc. So his family members saw the history he described and suddenly believed that he had been kidnapped. However, having been deceived before, they decided not to make the same mistake again, so they immediately replied and agreed to send the money on which day. At the same time, they reported to the Caojiadu Sixth District Police Station. Under the leadership of Chief District Inspector Xu, the detective team leader Liu Shaoqing, detectives Gan Youxin, Tang Bingxiang, Wu Rui, etc., and his family members all disguised themselves and went to Xujiahui according to the address. They wrapped the newspaper into 200 yuan of banknotes and placed it in the broken shoes. All the detectives were waiting nearby, ambushing for inspection. They waited for half a day and a night, but no one came to pick it up. There was no trace. Two days later, they went to see it, and the package was still in the shoes. Although his family members sighed in horror, they were still looking forward to it in Shanghai. The mystery in this is a hundred-fold and cannot be solved. Another month has passed, and there is still no news. It is expected that there is no hope of returning alive, so they returned to their hometown the day before yesterday and carried out the funeral rites.

Public Bus Accident 177

There are Streetcars in Front and Cars Behind

A Dilemma Causes Erratic Driving

Hitting a Tree Causes It to Fall and Break the Water Tank

Backing Up the Car Runs Over a Police Officer

At 9:55 yesterday morning, at the intersection of Sanyi Lane, east of Yangshupu Bridge, a Route 9 public bus, registered as 11508, driven by driver Xu A'er, was traveling from west to east. A streetcar in front of it was stopped at the station, preventing the public bus from moving forward. There was also a car following behind. Driver Xu A'er, seeing this situation, was in a dilemma. Wanting to avoid the car behind him, he quickly turned the steering wheel and drove to the side. However, he was flustered and driving erratically, causing the front of the car to hit the tree trunk on the side of the road. The tree fell down and broke a water tank. Xu then backed up the car. A police officer named Jin Dexin, number 3069, was coming on a bicycle and was unable to stop in time. He was run over by the public bus. The wheel rolled over Jin's face, and the blood and flesh were blurred, which was unbearable to watch. Even the bicycle became tile-like. A police officer number 179 arrived and copied the driver's number. The injured police officer was sent to the hospital for treatment by a fire truck. After arriving at the hospital, Jin was unconscious and feared for his life.

Wu Wenbing Throws Himself into the Huangpu River Because He Cannot Repay His Debts 178

Because of the Thick Clothes, It Was Not Easy to Sink

The Police Rescued Him and He Was Not Dead

At 0:40 yesterday morning, a middle-aged man threw himself into the Huangpu River in the dark of night at the Swire Wharf in the French Concession. Because of the thick clothes, he did not sink for a while. The police officers numbers 12 and 28 of the Water Police Station were patrolling on the bank of the Huangpu River. Hearing a sound in the Huangpu River, they immediately turned on the electric torch and saw the situation. They immediately rushed forward and rescued him from the water, celebrating his rebirth. The Huangpu wind blew and his face was pale. He was taken to the police station and given dry clothes to change into. After questioning, he said that his name was Wu Wenbing, 27 years old, from Shaoxing. He is now working in the Qingchun Socks Factory in Changan Lane, Wusong Road. Because he has heavy debts, amounting to more than 300 yuan, and cannot repay them, and the debt period is approaching and difficult to cope with, he threw himself into the Huangpu River to die. Shen Kuishan, who works in the same factory, is my best friend. After verifying the confession, the head of the police ordered Detective Wu Rongsheng to send him to his friend's place to find a way to provide relief after dawn.

Robbery at a Silk Weaving Factory – Detectives Capture Two Thieves 179

Neighbors Assist in Reporting to the Police

Detectives Rush to Encircle and Capture

Thieves Confess to Holding a Meeting

Stolen Foreign Currency Recovered

Hu Junzhi established a silk weaving factory at No. 75 Mingyuan Lane, Huade Road. At precisely 12:00 AM the previous evening, while distributing monthly salaries to the workers, four thieves suddenly broke into the factory through the back door. Each wielding a pistol, they first drove seven or eight workers downstairs into a room and locked them up. Then, two thieves specifically went upstairs and confined Hu in a pavilion room, before starting to rob. They stole a total of 350 yuan in banknotes, foreign currency, and small silver coins, along with three gold rings. Hu, noticing a window in the pavilion room, opened it and informed the neighbor, Lu Yinchao. Lu immediately telephoned the Yangshupu Police Station to report the incident. Detectives Zhang Degong and other Western detectives were dispatched to encircle and capture the thieves. By then, the thieves had already finished robbing and, having abandoned two pistols—one in a water basin and the other in a bamboo basket covered with cloth—they fled out through the back door. They happened to encounter the detectives. The two thieves in front managed to escape, but the two behind were captured. One was Shi Hongquan from Zhenjiang, and the other was Ding Yongqing from Jiangbei. Shi had 110 yuan of the stolen foreign currency hidden on his person, which was also completely recovered. They were taken back to the police station, and further inquiries were made at the silk weaving factory about the robbery. The two pistols left behind by the thieves were collected by the factory staff and handed over to the detectives, with twelve live bullets still in them. Later, according to the thieves' confession, their accomplices had fled to a certain location at the South Railway Station, but a search there yielded nothing. Yesterday morning, the police summoned the factory owner Hu Junzhi and the mechanic Chen Jiangang to escort Shi and Ding to the Special District Local Court. Judge Feng conducted the preliminary hearing, and the police lawyer Li Zhishan explained the case, requesting a postponement for further investigation of another case. Subsequently, Hu, Chen, and others described in detail the robbery and identified the captured men as those who had carried out the armed robbery at the scene. Under questioning, Shi and Ding claimed that the whole thing was initiated by a Liu surnamed individual who was still at large, and that a meeting had been held in front of the Great World entertainment center beforehand. They stated that besides what was found during the search, the rest of the stolen goods were taken away by Liu and a certain Yang. The court ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody pending further investigation.

Murderer Wu AYu Sentenced to Hanging 180

Wu AYu, a native of Pudong, was only twenty-four years old and worked as a carpenter. He had a dispute with Ji Ruiqing. On the evening of January 7th of the eighteenth year of the Republic, at 7:30 PM, he shot and killed Ji on Menala Road. The Huishi Police Station apprehended him and handed him over to the former Provisional Court, which sentenced him to life imprisonment. The case was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, which sent it back for retrial. The retrial resulted in a death sentence. Wu appealed, but his appeal was rejected. Now, upon receiving instructions from above to carry out the execution according to law, Judge Ge of the Special District Local Court ordered Wu to be brought to court yesterday afternoon. He asked Wu if he had any last words. Wu said that he had no face to see his family again and had no last words, but he requested some wine and food. Judge Ge ordered wine and food to be prepared. After he had finished drinking, the escorts were ordered to put him on a prison vehicle and take him directly to the execution ground at the Jiangsu Prison in Caohejing. Prosecutor Wu Shixin was appointed by the Procuratorate of the Local Court as the supervising officer of the execution. He ordered Police Chief Yang Deshan and Police Officer Chen Xihui to lead six executioners, Gu Hanqing, Xue Bingzhang, Zhu Wanyuan, Yin Daoxu, Zhang Chunshen, and Wu Xisheng, along with the necessary equipment, to travel to the prison in separate cars. Prosecutor Wu, along with Warden Huang Changmin and Clerk Qian Yinpei, took their positions on the official platform. Wu AYu was brought forward for questioning: (Question) Age 24, from Shanghai, residing in Qichang Inn, Pudong. (Question) Do you have anything to say? (Answer) Just execute me. (Question) Who is in your family so they can collect your body in the future? (Answer) Since I am already dead, whether they collect the body or not is not a problem, there's no need to ask. His attitude was so strong, he truly had no fear of the law. The order was given to execute. Under the command of Police Chief Yang, the executioners bound the prisoner to a wooden stake and slowly hanged him according to law. He died soon after. The examiner Xuan Zhiming certified his death, and the clerk supervised the sealing of the execution rope. The body was left exposed overnight, awaiting another examination the next day (today) before being collected.

Three years ago, my late father-in-law suffered from severe lung disease. At that time, a friend from Sichuan transported several coffins from Sichuan. They were of good quality and inexpensive. I persuaded him to purchase one. The value at that time was only over 1,000 yuan. The 7,000 yuan figure is a misrepresentation."
